❓:25. The cube shown has sides of length 2 units. Holes in the shape of a hemisphere are carved into each face of the cube. The six hemispheres are identical and their centres are at the centres of the faces of the cube. The holes are just large enough to touch the hole on each neighbouring face. What is the diameter of each hole?A 1B sqrt{2}C 2-sqrt{2}D 3-sqrt{2}E 3-sqrt{3}

The centers of these hemispheres are at the centers of the cube's faces. The problem is to determine the diameter of each hole such that the holes just touch each other on neighboring faces.1. Distance between centers of adjacent hemispheres: - Consider the centers of the front face (1, 1, 0) and the right face (2, 1, 1). The distance between these centers is calculated as: [ sqrt{(2 - 1)^2 + (1 - 1)^2 + (1 - 0)^2} = sqrt{1 + 0 + 1} = sqrt{2} ]2. Radius of hemispheres: - For the hemispheres to touch each other, the distance between their centers must be equal to twice the radius (since each hemisphere's radius extends towards the other). Let ( r ) be the radius of each hemisphere. Then: [ 2r = sqrt{2} implies r = frac{sqrt{2}}{2} ]3. Diameter of each hole: - The diameter is twice the radius: [ text{Diameter} = 2r = 2 times frac{sqrt{2}}{2} = sqrt{2} ]4. Verification: - The point of contact between two adjacent hemispheres is calculated to be (1.5, 1, 0.5), which lies on both hemispheres. Substituting this point into the equations of both hemispheres confirms that the distance from each center to this point is indeed ( frac{sqrt{2}}{2} ).Thus, the diameter of each hole is ( sqrt{2} ), corresponding to option B.[boxed{B}]]

🔑:SolUTIONBLet P and Q be the centres of two adjacent hemispheres. The faces on which these hemispheres are carved meet at an edge. Let M be the midpoint of that edge. Then M P=M Q=1. Also M P Q is a right-angled triangle since the two faces are perpendicular. By Pythagoras, M P^{2}+M Q^{2}=P Q^{2}, so P Q^{2}=1+1=2. Hence P Q=sqrt{2}, and P Q is equal to the sum of two radii, so is the same as the diameter of the hemispheres.

🔑:1. Identify the type of triangle: Given the sides of the triangle are (48), (55), and (73). We need to check if this is a right triangle. For a triangle with sides (a), (b), and (c) (where (c) is the largest side), it is a right triangle if (a^2 + b^2 = c^2). [ 48^2 + 55^2 = 2304 + 3025 = 5329 ] [ 73^2 = 5329 ] Since (48^2 + 55^2 = 73^2), the triangle is a right triangle with the hypotenuse (73).2. Calculate the area of the triangle: The area (A) of a right triangle can be calculated using the legs (a) and (b): [ A = frac{1}{2} times 48 times 55 = frac{1}{2} times 2640 = 1320 ]3. Find the altitude to the hypotenuse: The altitude (h) to the hypotenuse in a right triangle can be found using the area formula (A = frac{1}{2} times text{base} times text{height}). Here, the base is the hypotenuse (73): [ 1320 = frac{1}{2} times 73 times h ] [ 2640 = 73h ] [ h = frac{2640}{73} ]4. Simplify the fraction: The fraction (frac{2640}{73}) is already in its simplest form because (2640) and (73) are relatively prime (they have no common factors other than 1).5. Identify (a) and (b): Here, (a = 2640) and (b = 73).6. Calculate (a + b): [ a + b = 2640 + 73 = 2713 ]The final answer is (boxed{2713})

❓:Let AOB and COD be angles which can be identified by a rotation of the plane (such that rays OA and OC are identified). A circle is inscribed in each of these angles; these circles intersect at points E and F. Show that angles AOE and DOF are equal.

Rotation and Congruence: The angles ( angle AOB ) and ( angle COD ) are congruent due to the rotation. The inscribed circles in these angles are congruent and have the same radius.2. Centers of Inscribed Circles: The centers of the inscribed circles, ( I_1 ) and ( I_2 ), lie on the angle bisectors of ( angle AOB ) and ( angle COD ) respectively. These bisectors are separated by the rotation angle ( phi ).3. Radical Axis: The radical axis of the two circles is the line ( EF ), which is perpendicular to the line joining the centers ( I_1 ) and ( I_2 ). The radical axis ( EF ) is also the angle bisector of the angle formed by the arms ( OA ) and ( OD ).4. Symmetry and Angle Bisector: Since the radical axis ( EF ) is the angle bisector of ( angle AOD ), any point on ( EF ) is equidistant from ( OA ) and ( OD ). This symmetry implies that the angles ( angle AOE ) and ( angle DOF ) formed by the intersection points ( E ) and ( F ) with ( OA ) and ( OD ) are equal.5. Hence proved.Therefore, the key steps are:1. The two inscribed circles are congruent due to the rotation, so their radii are equal and their centers are equidistant from O.2. The intersection points E and F are such that OE = OF (due to rotation) and EI1 = FI2 = r.3. Triangles OEI1 and OFI2 are congruent by SSS, leading to angle EOI1 = angle FOI2.4. Adding these angles to the angle between OA and the bisector (theta/2) gives angle AOE and angle DOF, which are thus equal.Therefore, angles AOE and DOF are equal.Final Answerboxed{angle AOE = angle DOF}</think>Given two angles ( angle AOB ) and ( angle COD ) related by a rotation of the plane around point ( O ) such that rays ( OA ) and ( OC ) are identified, we need to show that angles ( angle AOE ) and ( angle DOF ) are equal, where ( E ) and ( F ) are the intersection points of the circles inscribed in each angle.1. Rotation and Congruence: - The rotation maps ( OA ) to ( OC ) and ( OB ) to ( OD ), making ( angle AOB ) and ( angle COD ) congruent. - The inscribed circles in ( angle AOB ) and ( angle COD ) are congruent because the rotation preserves distances and angles.2. Intersection Points: - The inscribed circles intersect at points ( E ) and ( F ). Due to the rotation, ( E ) and ( F ) are symmetric with respect to the rotation. This implies ( OE = OF ) and the radii of the circles are equal.3. Congruent Triangles: - Consider triangles ( OEI_1 ) and ( OFI_2 ), where ( I_1 ) and ( I_2 ) are the centers of the inscribed circles in ( angle AOB ) and ( angle COD ) respectively. - These triangles are congruent by SSS (Side-Side-Side) congruence: ( OE = OF ), ( OI_1 = OI_2 ) (distance from ( O ) to the centers), and ( EI_1 = FI_2 ) (radii of the congruent circles).4. Angle Equality: - The congruence of triangles ( OEI_1 ) and ( OFI_2 ) implies ( angle EOI_1 = angle FOI_2 ). - The angles ( angle AOE ) and ( angle DOF ) are each composed of half the original angle (( theta/2 )) plus the respective angles ( angle EOI_1 ) and ( angle FOI_2 ). Since these angles are equal, ( angle AOE = angle DOF ).Thus, we conclude that angles ( angle AOE ) and ( angle DOF ) are equal.[boxed{angle AOE = angle DOF}]]

🔑:1. Identify the given elements and transformations: - We have two angles ( angle AOB ) and ( angle COD ) formed by the rotation of the plane such that rays ( OA ) and ( OC ) are identified. - Two circles are inscribed in these angles, intersecting at points ( E ) and ( F ). - We need to show that ( angle AOE = angle DOF ).2. Consider the composition of transformations: - First, consider the axial symmetry with respect to the bisector of angle ( angle AOD ). This symmetry will reflect any point on one side of the bisector to the other side. - Second, consider the inversion with respect to point ( O ). Inversion with respect to a point ( O ) maps any point ( P ) to a point ( P' ) such that ( OP cdot OP' = r^2 ), where ( r ) is the radius of the circle of inversion.3. Apply the transformations to the circles: - The axial symmetry with respect to the bisector of ( angle AOD ) will map the inscribed circles to themselves because the bisector is a line of symmetry for both angles. - The inversion with respect to ( O ) will swap the two circles because inversion preserves the angles and maps circles to circles.4. Analyze the effect on points ( E ) and ( F ): - Since the inversion swaps the circles, it will also swap the intersection points ( E ) and ( F ). - Therefore, under the composition of axial symmetry and inversion, points ( E ) and ( F ) are swapped.5. Conclude the isogonality: - Since ( E ) and ( F ) are swapped by the composition of axial symmetry and inversion, the lines ( OE ) and ( OF ) are isogonal with respect to ( angle AOD ). This means that ( angle AOE ) and ( angle DOF ) are equal.[boxed{angle AOE = angle DOF}]

External Angle of the Necklace: When two pentagons are connected, the angle outside the pentagons (the external angle of the necklace) is: [ 360^circ - 2 times 108^circ = 144^circ ] The external angle of the necklace polygon, which is the angle turned when moving from one pentagon to the next, is: [ 180^circ - 144^circ = 36^circ ]3. Number of Plates: The total external angles around a closed loop must sum to (360^circ). Therefore, the number of pentagons (N) is: [ N = frac{360^circ}{36^circ} = 10 ]Thus, the number of plates forming the necklace is (boxed{10}).]

🔑:The internal angle of a regular pentagon measures 108^{circ}. Therefore, the internal angle of the polygon determined by the necklace measures 360^{circ}-108^{circ}-108^{circ}=144^{circ}. We must then find n such thatfrac{180^{circ}(n-2)}{n}=144^{circ}Solving this equation, we get n=10. Therefore, ten plates form the necklace.

First, we rewrite the original equation in terms of (y). The second term (frac{5x + 5}{x^2 + 2}) can be factored as (frac{5(x + 1)}{x^2 + 2}). Since (y = frac{x^2 + 2}{x + 1}), the reciprocal of (y) is (frac{x + 1}{x^2 + 2}). 🔑:To solve the equation frac{x^2+2}{x+1} + frac{5x+5}{x^2+2} = 6 using the method of substitution, we follow these steps:1. Recognize that the given equation can be rewritten by factoring out 5 from the numerator of the second fraction: [frac{x^2+2}{x+1} + frac{5(x+1)}{x^2+2} = 6.]2. Let frac{x^2+2}{x+1} = y. This implies that frac{x+1}{x^2+2} = frac{1}{y} because inverting both sides of the equation frac{x^2+2}{x+1} = y gives us the reciprocal relationship.3. Substitute the value of y and its reciprocal into the original equation:[y + frac{5}{y} = 6.]4. To find a polynomial equation in terms of y, we multiply each term by y to eliminate the fraction and get:[y^2 + 5 = 6y.]5. Rearranging the terms to set the equation to 0, we obtain:[y^2 - 6y + 5 = 0.]Therefore, by using the method of substitution and letting frac{x^2+2}{x+1} = y, the original equation can be transformed into the polynomial equation boxed{y^2 - 6y + 5 = 0}.
